The Decks of #WOTCSTAFF
=======================



 Posted in **Feature**
 on October 9, 2018 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/wizards_authorpic_larger.jpg)
By Wizards of the Coast











Some of *Magic*'s biggest fans work right here at Wizards of the Coast. Many of us were drawn to helping make the game that we love.


Thanks to an idea on Twitter from [@CheshirePlays](http://www.twitter.com/CheshirePlays) and [@TolarianCollege](http://www.twitter.com/TolarianCollege), we thought we'd show you just a few of the ways some of us here at Wizards of the Coast enjoy *Magic*. From Spikey Modern decks to Casual Cat decks, we've got a little bit of everything.


Enjoy our most enjoyable decks from the people who make *Magic*, described in their own words.


Melissa DeTora's Vaevictis Asmadi, the DireÂ Brawl
=================================================


This is my Brawl deck. I built it for Gen Con and had lots of fun meeting other Brawl players and playing. Case Kiyonaga (contractor on the delta team and a good friend) inspired me to go with Vaevictus as the commander.







#### DeTora's Dire Brawl


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

 Vaevictis Asmadi, the Dire

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Vaevictis+Asmadi%2C+the+Dire)

















Andrew Brown's Modern Ad Nauseam
================================


This is my favorite Modern deck Ad Nauseam. I love playing traditional, fair decks in Standard and Limited. But in older formats I really enjoy changing it up and playing something particularly unconventional. I've played this deck at countless premiere events and racked up some sweet finishes. There's nothing more satisfying than having your entire deck in your hand.







#### Brown's Modern Ad Nauseam


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

Elaine Chase's Singleton Cats
=============================


If you follow Elaine Chase on [Twitter](https://twitter.com/ElaineChase), this should come as no surprise. This is the deck she plays when she feels the need to curl up in a small box or knock a glass off the table.


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Chase_Cats.jpg)







#### Elaine Chase's Singleton Cats


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

Ethan Fleischer's Reki, the History of KamigawaÂ Commander
=========================================================


I have around 30 Commander decks; it's my favorite format. The deck that is consistently the most fun is my [Reki, the History of Kamigawa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reki%2C+the+History+of+Kamigawa) deck. My favorite way to win games of Commander is with cards that normally would be too weak to consider but, in the context of a specific deck, become powerful enough to defeat an entire table. Reki turns every legendary card into a cantrip, which vastly increases the range of potentially viable cards. The drawback, of course, is that you only have access to mono-green and colorless cards. This means that I had to look hard for cards to interact with my opponents (other than the standard interaction of a tide of giant green creatures slamming into the red zone). It's fun beating players with cards they may never have heard of!


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Fleischer_Reki.jpg)







#### Reki, the History of Kamigawa


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

Aaron Forsythe's Family Deck
============================


When I want to play *Magic* for fun, I usually fire up the *MTG Arena* Open Beta. When I want to play with other humans for fun, I'll play casual games with my daughtersâeither 1v1, three-person free-for-all, or [Two-Headed Giant](https://magic.wizards.com/en/game-info/gameplay/formats/two-headed-giant). The decks we use are reminiscent of the style of deck I fell in love with the game playing: "What can I build from the contents of these booster packs?" My kids and I will open a box or a bunch of packs, they'll pick out the cards that excite them, and I'll make a deck around it.


My oldest daughter gravitated toward [The Gitrog Monster](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Gitrog+Monster), Liliana, and Emrakul from the *Shadows over Innistrad* and *Eldritch Moon* packs we opened a few years ago, and this black-green delirium deck is still her favorite today. The real star of the show is the [Chittering Host](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chittering+Host) made by melding [Graf Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Graf+Rats) and [Midnight Scavengers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Midnight+Scavengers).


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Forsythe_Delirium.jpg)

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gnarlwood+Dryad)

















Alli Medwin's M'Odo, the Gnarled Oracle Commander
=================================================


This isn't my favorite deck, but it is my *newest* deck. After creating M'Odo through Wizards' Heroes of the Realm award, I knew I needed to make a Commander deck with it. But it's way too easy to combo off; all you need is a single 1-CMC creature, a single 2-CMC creature, etc. That kind of consistency seems counter to the spirit of the card, and certainly counter to my sense of fun. So, I took on the deck-building rule of "no creature cards," with the intention of using the creature cards in my opponents' decks instead. I ended up breaking that rule for Ulamog so I could get some powerful reshuffling, but I accept that I simply need to never activate that ability targeting myself (not a problem; there are way more fun things to do with eleven mana). This deck is totally untested and probably missing a few staples that I "need" to have, but this is what I'm taking to my next Commander game.


![image of M'odo](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/Mwy2vcEKDk.png)


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Medwin_Modo.jpg)

Gavin Verhey's Brawl and Pauper Decks
=====================================


Hey all! Gavin Verhey, senior *Magic* designer and product architect here.


One of the many exciting things I get to do in my role is explore new and burgeoning formats. I love designing, crafting, and, of course, deck building for them. Today, I want to highlight two of my decks which are doing exactly that.


The first is in a format you have probably heard plenty about lately: Brawl!


Recently, we had the first ever Brawl Championship at Grand Prix Richmond! I flew out to Richmond myself for the tournament and wanted to play something fun. So, I built up [Arcades, the Strategist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arcades%2C+the+Strategist). There were tons of different legendary commanders in the tournament, but I was the only Arcades. Fielding cards like [Wall of Mist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Mist) and [Suspicious Bookcase](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Suspicious+Bookcase), my deck was full of oddballs . . .


. . . and it ended up being some of the most fun I've *ever* had playing *Magic*!


Beating down with my army of defenders put a huge smile on my (and many of my opponents') faces, and it turns out it was quite strong too, as I advanced through five rounds to make the Top 4 players, losing only to the eventual winner who was playing [Firesong and Sunspeaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firesong+and+Sunspeaker). There are some surprisingly great "Wall [tribal](http://magic.wizards.com/en/articles/archive/making-magic/cats-2017-08-07#tribal)" cards in Standard in addition to Arcades, like [Mentor of the Meek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mentor+of+the+Meek), [Tetsuko Umezawa, Fugitive](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tetsuko+Umezawa%2C+Fugitive), and [Slaughter the Strong](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughter+the+Strong).







#### Gavin Verhey's Arcades, the Strategist


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Arcades%2C+the+Strategist)

















The second deck I'd like to highlight is in a very different format, but another one I've been enjoying: Pauper!


As Pauper was the center of plenty of community discussion and was growing in popularity thanks to community members like the Professor and Alex Ullman, I hopped in at the start of the year to see what the buzz was about and do some research on the format.


It was sort of like calling up a bunch of friends you haven't hung out with in a while and getting together. I decided on one of my favorite archetypes in *Magic*: Blue-Black Teachings!


Hey [Mystical Teachings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mystical+Teachings), how's it going? [Accumulated Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Accumulated+Knowledge)âwow, it's been ages, what are you up to these days? [Chainer's Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chainer%27s+Edict), you still doing the whole sacrificing creatures thing?


I've played this deck a bunch online and in real life, done quite well with it, and have a version I'm really happy with. I have more ways to turbo out a [Gurmag Angler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gurmag+Angler) than most builds, using [Ash Barrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ash+Barrens) and [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain). And while it's true that Gurmag is a nonbo with [Accumulated Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Accumulated+Knowledge) and [Mystical Teachings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mystical+Teachings), having both has been worth the synergy hit.

Blake Rasmussen's Grixis Canadian Highlander
============================================


Singleton formats are my favorite. I love so many cards that playing four-ofs just eats up too much space. The hardest part of building any deck for me is cutting my darlings. So, I just want to play them all.


That's why my favorite decks tend to be Commander or Canadian Highlander decks. I have a Bant deck that has existed for maybe a decade, though it has morphed from all the combos (back when [Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fastbond) was legal, for instance) to all the good stuff (many of those cards still remain) to an Enchantress deck when I finally pulled the plug on my *Legends* [Rubinia Soulsinger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubinia+Soulsinger) and replaced her with [Tuvasa the Sunlit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tuvasa+the+Sunlit). The deck is home to my precious [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat), which I just acquired, and the first [Mana Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Crypt) I ever got (I now have three).


And that's not even my favorite deck.


I'm going to share two decks with you today. As you can see from my decks, I'm greedy like that.


I have two decks that vie for being my favorite, though, if I'm honest, I know which one I would save first if my house went up in flames.


And somehow, it's not my almost all-foil [Azami, Lady of Scrolls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azami%2C+Lady+of+Scrolls) Commander deck. Despite how much I enjoy having a foil [Foil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Foil).


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Blake_Azami.jpg)

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Azami%2C+Lady+of+Scrolls)

















No, my favorite deck has all my favorite cards. Except for [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat), I guess. Even I can't play everything.


It has [Cruel Ultimatum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cruel+Ultimatum). [Mulldrifter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mulldrifter). [Library of Alexandria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Library+of+Alexandria). [Riptide Lab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Riptide+Lab). [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). [Mana Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Drain). [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven). [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). All the Jaces (well, almost all the Jaces). [Spellseeker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellseeker) and [Search for Azcanta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Azcanta). [Hymn to freakin' Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach).


But I also get the warm and fuzzies from the nuts and bolts of the deck. [Impulse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Impulse) is a nostalgic favorite of mine. [Desolate Lighthouse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desolate+Lighthouse) makes me happy. [Electrolyze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Electrolyze) is pure value. Textless [Damnation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Damnation) is just cool. Same with [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command), at least for those of us who know all the modes by heart.


If you're not sure what Canadian Highlander is, [check here](https://canadianhighlander.wordpress.com/). If you already know the format (or after you learned about it just now, I guess), you can see my deck's point cards at the top of this photo.


![](https://media.wizards.com/2018/images/daily/FEAT20181009_Blake_CHL.jpg)

#####
